# Final JEPA Candidate Priority 2026-05-27

This table combines the JEPA hidden-block candidate metrics with the actual-public-anchor ranker.
The ranker anchors each inverse-fit public scenario/mask combo to the observed stage2 public LB instead of trusting raw pseudo-public CE as an absolute score.

## Calibration Caveat

- raw05 actual public LB is 0.5775263072, but the ranker scores it at 0.5779059944; it is pessimistic by 0.0003238423.
- direct JEPA latent residual actual public LB is 0.5812273278, but the ranker scores it at 0.5802891189; it is optimistic by 0.0012342624.
- Therefore, use `actual_anchor_score_final` as a public-consistency filter, not as proof that a candidate beats raw05.

## Local LB Uncertainty Caveat

- `analysis_outputs/local_lb_proxy_uncertainty_decomposition.py` reruns the local public-LB proxy as an uncertainty diagnostic over the six known public submissions.
- Best leave-one-public-anchor model remains `loocv_ridge_abs_axes_a1`, with MAE `0.0003184931` and RMSE `0.0004029881`.
- Best-model known-anchor absolute error p50/p80/p90/max is `0.0003380359` / `0.0005912615` / `0.0006026900` / `0.0006141185`; raw05 itself is over-predicted by `0.0006141185`.
- No candidate is locally resolved under the strict rule. `1067` negative-delta candidates are still below the 5%-of-MAE practical resolution floor (`0.0000159247`).
- Therefore ranks 10-16 are structural/JEPA information probes, not locally proven public-LB improvements. Keep `submission_raw05_jepa_anchorrobust_graft_e40a9b92.csv` as the conservative first submit probe; use lowbad/direct variants only as follow-up probes.

## 2026-05-28 A2C8 And Direct-Label Update

Observed public anchor update:

- `analysis_outputs/submission_frontier_cvjepa_refine_a2c8d2c8.csv`: public `0.577439321`, current observed best.
- a2c8 improves raw05 by only `0.0000869862`; the remaining gap to 0.54 is `0.037439321`.
- This proves the current JEPA/raw05-compatible micro-refine branch is directionally valid but far too low-amplitude to reach 0.54.

New direct hidden-label inverse branch:

- script: `analysis_outputs/public_lb_direct_label_inverse7.py`
- LOO diagnostic: `analysis_outputs/public_lb_direct_label_inverse7_loocv.py`
- selected candidates: `analysis_outputs/public_lb_direct_label_inverse7_selected.csv`
- leave-one-anchor-out train-best mean absolute error: `0.000599`
- oracle-best mean absolute error: `0.000363`

Interpretation:

- The direct inverse can construct soft labels that explain all known public anchors, but the selector is underidentified. Its expected improvements are similar in size to the LOO error, so these files are diagnostic probes, not conservative replacements for a2c8.
- If a direct-label probe improves public LB, the next cycle should hard-pivot to hidden public subset/label solving. If it worsens, keep direct-label only as a regularizer and continue with JEPA block/count energy gates.

Current next-submit recommendation:

1. `analysis_outputs/submission_directrob_29ffe34b.csv`
   - updated first direct-label diagnostic after LOO robust selector.
   - source `frac0.40_rep009`, source LOO MAE `0.000578`, L2O MAE `0.000532`, target `all`, strength `0.5`, cap `0.055`.
   - robust delta vs a2c8 `-0.000548`, mean abs move `0.002696`, actual-anchor proxy `0.577760`.
   - This replaces `submission_directlbl_8b33d6dd.csv` as the first direct-label test because its source mask generalizes better in both leave-one-anchor and leave-two-anchor validation.

2. `analysis_outputs/submission_directrob_93b1b685.csv`
   - structured subject-contiguous version of the same test.
   - source `frac0.40_rep052`, source LOO MAE `0.000676`, L2O MAE `0.000607`, target `all`, strength `0.5`, cap `0.055`.
   - robust delta `-0.000551`, mean abs move `0.002539`, actual-anchor proxy `0.577763`.

3. `analysis_outputs/submission_directrob_9e356350.csv`
   - best actual-anchor proxy among selected robust candidates.
   - source `frac0.50_rep142`, source LOO MAE `0.000751`, strength `0.5`, cap `0.040`.
   - actual-anchor proxy `0.577743`; more upside, but source selector risk is higher.

4. `analysis_outputs/submission_directrob_93de02d3.csv`
   - high-information larger-move probe.
   - source LOO MAE `0.000751`, L2O MAE `0.000671`.
   - robust delta `-0.000912`, mean abs move `0.004557`, actual-anchor proxy `0.577773`.
   - Use after a safer robust direct-label probe confirms the direction.

5. `analysis_outputs/submission_inverse7blend_1040423d.csv`
   - safer a2c8-adjacent blend control from the previous inverse7 branch. Smaller expected gain, but less dependent on exact hidden labels.

Do not interpret any local estimate around `0.5766~0.5768` as an actual LB forecast. It is an inverse-scenario score. The trustworthy statement is narrower: these probes test whether the current public hidden-label direction is real.

Robust-selector artifacts:

- `analysis_outputs/public_lb_direct_label_inverse7_l2ocv.py`
- `analysis_outputs/public_lb_direct_label_inverse7_l2ocv_report.md`

## 2026-05-28 Direct-Label Consensus Energy Update

New LeJEPA-style consensus branch:

- script: `analysis_outputs/public_lb_direct_label_consensus_energy.py`
- report: `analysis_outputs/public_lb_direct_label_consensus_energy_report.md`
- selected: `analysis_outputs/public_lb_direct_label_consensus_energy_selected.csv`
- actual-anchor audit: `analysis_outputs/public_lb_direct_label_consensus_energy_actual_anchor.csv`
- selected candidates: `28`, integrity checks pass.

This branch aggregates pseudo-label cells from multiple LOO/L2O-stable direct-label solutions and assigns low energy only when sources agree on direction with low dispersion. It is a hidden-label regularizer, not a new local CV feature.

Important correction to candidate ranking:

- Robust inverse score alone prefers broad all-target consensus moves, but actual-anchor stress rejects them.
- Example rejected broad moves:
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_directcons_1d5b6f39.csv`: all target, actual-anchor `0.579190`
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_directcons_0b3f77c3.csv`: all target, actual-anchor `0.578529`
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_directcons_95be47ec.csv`: all target, actual-anchor `0.579207`
- The consensus family that survives public-axis stress is Q3/S4 only:
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_directcons_de1d6b6d.csv`: target `q3_s4`, gate `energy_broad`, strength `0.45`, cap `0.060`, actual-anchor `0.577802`, robust delta vs a2c8 `-0.000477`, mean abs move `0.003748`
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_directcons_8a0ae0b0.csv`: target `q3_s4`, gate `energy_balanced`, strength `0.45`, cap `0.060`, actual-anchor `0.577803`, robust delta `-0.000476`, mean abs move `0.003722`
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_directcons_bf4f6c46.csv`: target `q3_s4`, gate `energy_strict`, strength `0.45`, cap `0.060`, actual-anchor `0.577806`, robust delta `-0.000469`, mean abs move `0.003605`

Submission decision:

- Do not replace the first direct-label diagnostic with all-target consensus. Those files are public-axis failure probes.
- Keep `analysis_outputs/submission_directrob_29ffe34b.csv` as the first direct-label submit because it has the best LOO/L2O source evidence and actual-anchor proxy `0.577760`.
- Keep `analysis_outputs/submission_directrob_93b1b685.csv` as the structured control, actual-anchor proxy `0.577763`.
- Use `analysis_outputs/submission_directcons_de1d6b6d.csv` only as a follow-up Q3/S4 consensus control. It tests whether cross-source energy agreement transfers better than single-source directrob, but its actual-anchor proxy is weaker than the top directrob probes.
- Avoid `analysis_outputs/submission_directcons_de6f03cb.csv` as first submit despite strong robust inverse delta; actual-anchor stress is `0.577863`, worse than a2c8 control.

Strategic interpretation:

- The useful hidden-axis is not “all targets on high consensus rows.” It is target-specific and concentrated in Q3/S4.
- This explains why earlier broad JEPA residual and direct latent probes failed public LB: they were likely right on some hidden cells but wrong on too many non-Q3/S4 or non-public-axis cells.
- The 0.54 bottleneck remains hidden-label/subset identification. Consensus-energy improves the gate, but its safe moves are still around `0.0036~0.0037` mean absolute probability movement, not the larger amplitude needed for a step-change.

## 2026-05-28 JEPA-Regularized Sparse Direct Solver Update

New sparse solver branch:

- script: `analysis_outputs/jepa_regularized_sparse_direct_solver.py`
- report: `analysis_outputs/jepa_regularized_sparse_direct_solver_report.md`
- scan: `analysis_outputs/jepa_regularized_sparse_direct_solver_scan.csv`
- selected: `analysis_outputs/jepa_regularized_sparse_direct_solver_selected.csv`
- actual-anchor audit: `analysis_outputs/jepa_regularized_sparse_direct_solver_actual_anchor.csv`
- selected candidates: `32`, row/key/probability/NaN integrity checks pass.

Method:

- Start from observed-best `a2c8`.
- Build sparse row-target moves from direct-label consensus cells.
- Mix four JEPA/direct signals:
  - directrob source moves
  - Q3/S4 consensus moves
  - JEPA block/count/public-block directions
  - sequence motif directions
- Gate by consensus energy/agreement/source count and target mask.
- Optionally project away from rejected public axes: broad all-target consensus, latent residual, Q2-forced latent, and ordinal-Q drift.

Key result:

- The solver found a new actual-anchor frontier with mean move `0.0045~0.0068`, above the previous directrob/consensus band.
- Best actual-anchor sparse row:
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_sparsejepa_f4657144.csv`
  - signal `sparse_fusion`, target `all`, gate `q3s4_edge`, strength `0.75`, cap `0.080`
  - actual-anchor `0.577698`, robust delta vs a2c8 `-0.000941`, mean abs move `0.006176`
- Safer no-Q2 sparse row:
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_sparsejepa_3cfdf64a.csv`
  - signal `sparse_fusion`, target `no_q2`, gate `q3s4_edge`, strength `0.75`, cap `0.080`
  - actual-anchor `0.577706`, robust delta `-0.000878`, mean abs move `0.005520`
- Q3/stage-specific control:
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_sparsejepa_a2d8107a.csv`
  - target `q3_s2_s3_s4`, actual-anchor `0.577727`, robust delta `-0.000563`, mean abs move `0.003700`

Decision update:

- If optimizing next public information and accepting risk, submit `submission_sparsejepa_f4657144.csv`.
- If avoiding the known broad/all-target failure mode, submit `submission_sparsejepa_3cfdf64a.csv` first. It gives up only `0.000008` actual-anchor proxy versus the all-target best and removes Q2 movement.
- Use `submission_sparsejepa_a2d8107a.csv` as the target-specific Q3/stage control.
- The anti-axis projection variants did not win this round; projecting away from rejected axes reduced move amplitude and worsened actual-anchor proxy. Treat anti-axis as a guardrail, not the current score frontier.

Strategic interpretation:

- This is the first branch that increases move amplitude beyond `0.005` while improving the actual-anchor proxy over both `directrob_29ffe34b` (`0.577760`) and `directcons_de1d6b6d` (`0.577802`).
- It is still not a proven public LB forecast. The best rows use broad all-row gates, so public submission is needed to decide whether this is a real hidden-label direction or another inverse overfit.
- For the 0.54 objective, this is more relevant than another raw05 micro-refine because it finally tests a larger JEPA-regularized hidden-label move.

## 2026-05-28 JEPA Sparse Anchor-CV Audit Update

Additional audit:

- script: `analysis_outputs/jepa_sparse_anchor_cv_audit.py`
- report: `analysis_outputs/jepa_sparse_anchor_cv_audit_report.md`
- summary: `analysis_outputs/jepa_sparse_anchor_cv_audit_summary.csv`
- detail: `analysis_outputs/jepa_sparse_anchor_cv_audit_detail.csv`

Method:

- Retrain direct-label hidden-label fits while leaving out known public anchors.
- Score sparse JEPA candidates under those fold-specific hidden-label fits.
- Use both LOO and L2O folds, with `train_best1`, `train_best5`, `structured_best3`, and `low_error_best5` selector policies.
- Treat `low_error_best5` as an oracle-like diagnostic only; it is not allowed to drive the submission decision by itself.

Key combined LOO/L2O stability:

- `analysis_outputs/submission_sparsejepa_f43ea825.csv`: CV delta mean `-0.000869`, p90 `-0.000750`, worst `-0.000411`, win rate `1.0`, actual-anchor `0.577727`, mean move `0.007326`.
- `analysis_outputs/submission_sparsejepa_282e9546.csv`: CV delta mean `-0.000741`, p90 `-0.000644`, worst `-0.000367`, actual-anchor `0.577708`, mean move `0.006783`.
- `analysis_outputs/submission_sparsejepa_f4657144.csv`: CV delta mean `-0.000721`, p90 `-0.000629`, worst `-0.000364`, actual-anchor `0.577698`, mean move `0.006176`.
- `analysis_outputs/submission_sparsejepa_3cfdf64a.csv`: CV delta mean `-0.000665`, p90 `-0.000580`, worst `-0.000341`, actual-anchor `0.577706`, mean move `0.005520`.
- Control `analysis_outputs/submission_directrob_29ffe34b.csv`: CV delta mean `-0.000592`, p90 `-0.000520`, worst `-0.000257`.
- Control `analysis_outputs/submission_raw_timeline_jepa_rescue_strict_scale0p5.csv`: CV delta mean `+0.000131`, p90 `+0.000189`, worst `+0.000224`.

Decision update:

- The sparse candidates are not only all-anchor inverse artifacts. They remain directionally negative after leaving out public anchors.
- `f43ea825` is the strongest CV-stability/high-information probe, but its actual-anchor proxy is weaker and the move is larger/all-target.
- `f4657144` remains the best actual-anchor sparse candidate and is also anchor-CV stable.
- `3cfdf64a` remains the most defensible first sparse public probe because it removes Q2 while keeping nearly the same actual-anchor score and strong LOO/L2O stability.
- The selector absolute error around `0.00056` is still comparable to the candidate deltas, so public submission is required before claiming real LB improvement.

## 2026-05-28 Sparse Scale-Ladder Stress Update

New scale stress branch:

- script: `analysis_outputs/jepa_sparse_scale_ladder_stress.py`
- report: `analysis_outputs/jepa_sparse_scale_ladder_stress_report.md`
- scan: `analysis_outputs/jepa_sparse_scale_ladder_stress_scan.csv`
- anchor-CV summary: `analysis_outputs/jepa_sparse_scale_ladder_stress_cv_summary.csv`
- selected: `analysis_outputs/jepa_sparse_scale_ladder_stress_selected.csv`

Method:

- Take the strongest sparse JEPA/direct-label directions as logit vectors from a2c8.
- Extrapolate them by scale instead of searching new cells.
- Test full, no-Q2, top-absolute, and high-energy variants.
- Re-run actual-anchor stress and honest LOO/L2O anchor-CV policies.

Key breakpoints:

- `f465_actual_best` full direction improves honest anchor-CV as scale increases:
  - scale `1.00`: actual-anchor `0.577698`, honest CV delta `-0.000755`, move `0.006176`
  - scale `1.30`: actual-anchor `0.577724`, honest CV delta `-0.000919`, move `0.008027`
  - scale `1.50`: actual-anchor `0.577757`, honest CV delta `-0.001013`, move `0.009260`
  - scale `1.75`: actual-anchor `0.577818`, honest CV delta `-0.001113`, move `0.010801`
  - scale `2.00`: actual-anchor `0.577899`, honest CV delta `-0.001193`, move `0.012342`
- This is the clearest evidence so far that the bottleneck may be under-scaling of the correct hidden-label direction, not only target leakage.
- Public-axis risk starts becoming material around scale `1.75~2.00`: CV keeps improving, but actual-anchor proxy degrades.

New larger-move candidates:

- `analysis_outputs/submission_sparseladder_89817541.csv`: `f465_actual_best`, full, scale `1.50`, actual-anchor `0.577757`, honest CV delta `-0.001013`, mean move `0.009260`.
- `analysis_outputs/submission_sparseladder_f1ee16b0.csv`: `f465_actual_best`, no-Q2, scale `1.50`, actual-anchor `0.577758`, honest CV delta `-0.000934`, mean move `0.008276`.
- `analysis_outputs/submission_sparseladder_b01acaa1.csv`: `282_consensus_directrob`, full, scale `1.30`, actual-anchor `0.577746`, honest CV delta `-0.000935`, mean move `0.008816`.
- `analysis_outputs/submission_sparseladder_3be0b7a3.csv`: `282_consensus_directrob`, energy_top60, scale `1.50`, actual-anchor `0.577764`, honest CV delta `-0.000937`, mean move `0.007001`.

Decision update:

- For a conservative first sparse submit, keep `analysis_outputs/submission_sparsejepa_3cfdf64a.csv`.
- For a high-information larger-move submit, use `analysis_outputs/submission_sparseladder_f1ee16b0.csv` first if Q2 risk control matters, or `analysis_outputs/submission_sparseladder_89817541.csv` if maximizing scale signal is the priority.
- The 0.54 path should now focus on identifying whether scale `1.5` public-transfers. If it improves, the next family should solve for still larger cell-specific scale; if it fails, the hidden direction is right locally but contaminated by public/private target leakage.

## 2026-05-28 Adaptive Sparse Scale Solver Update

New adaptive branch:

- script: `analysis_outputs/jepa_adaptive_sparse_scale_solver.py`
- report: `analysis_outputs/jepa_adaptive_sparse_scale_solver_report.md`
- scan: `analysis_outputs/jepa_adaptive_sparse_scale_solver_scan.csv`
- actual-anchor audit: `analysis_outputs/jepa_adaptive_sparse_scale_solver_actual_anchor.csv`
- anchor-CV summary: `analysis_outputs/jepa_adaptive_sparse_scale_solver_cv_summary.csv`
- selected: `analysis_outputs/jepa_adaptive_sparse_scale_solver_selected.csv`

Method:

- Start from the sparse JEPA/direct-label logit directions.
- Replace uniform scale with cell-wise scale factors based on target profile, consensus energy, subject block, and sequence position.
- Test no-Q2, stage-boost, Q3/stage, high-energy, public-subject, id01/id02 early, and late-block profiles.

Result:

- Adaptive profiles improve honest anchor-CV but worsen actual-anchor versus uniform scale-ladder.
- Best adaptive actual-anchor:
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_adaptjepa_c10b7ebd.csv`
  - source `f465_actual_best`, target `noq2`, energy `energy_strong`, block `all_rows`, scale `1.50`
  - actual-anchor `0.577798`, honest CV delta `-0.001178`, mean move `0.008808`
- Best guarded adaptive:
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_adaptjepa_8fabe65a.csv`
  - source `3cf_noq2_safe`, target `noq2`, energy `energy_strong`, block `late_subject_blocks`, scale `1.50`
  - actual-anchor `0.577806`, honest CV delta `-0.001192`, mean move `0.008838`
- Uniform scale-ladder remains better on public-axis:
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_sparseladder_89817541.csv`: actual-anchor `0.577757`, honest CV delta `-0.001013`, mean move `0.009260`
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_sparseladder_f1ee16b0.csv`: actual-anchor `0.577758`, honest CV delta `-0.000934`, mean move `0.008276`

Decision update:

- Do not promote adaptive candidates above uniform scale-ladder for next public submit.
- Adaptive no-Q2/high-energy profiles are useful diagnostics: they show stronger hidden-label fit but more public-axis leakage.
- The current sparse direction behaves almost one-dimensionally under public-anchor stress. The next public decision should test uniform scale transfer first, then use adaptive solvers only after the public response identifies which target/block is leaking.

## Q3 Stress Counterweight Addendum

Counterweight search keeps the Q3 stress signal and blends non-Q3 target blocks toward low-bad/strict candidates. It did not beat the raw actual-anchor peak, but it sharply lowers bad-axis exposure while staying near the Q3 stress frontier.

## Q3 Stress Counterweight Local Addendum

Local counterweight refine keeps the Q3/S4 stress base, searches nearby non-Q3/S4 target profiles, and adds very-low-bad candidates so the JEPA signal can be tested with a tighter bad-axis guardrail.

## Context-Target Energy Gate Addendum

This addendum uses the I-JEPA context-target idea directly: non-Q3/S context predictions define the context block, Q3/S4 defines the target block, and counterweight rows are kept when they lower learned compatibility energy. The branch is a guardrail/diagnostic branch, not the current actual-anchor frontier.

## Energy-Constrained Frontier Addendum

## Energyfront Microrefine Addendum

This branch performs a second-stage local stitch inside the energyfront manifold. The main value is not a new actual-anchor minimum, but a sharp bad-axis collapse while staying near the frontier.

## Efmicro Row-Gate Refine Addendum

This branch tightens the row-level gate around the energyfront/micro frontier. It does not recover the actual-anchor frontier, but it creates the strongest bad-axis collapse seen in the raw05-compatible JEPA branch.

## EFGate Backoff Frontier Addendum

This branch interpolates between the actual-anchor micro/energyfront frontier and the efgate low-bad diagnostics. It is useful as a middle point: weaker actual-anchor than micro, but cleaner posterior/bad-axis than the frontier.

## SIGReg-Gated Microrefine Addendum

This branch applies the LeJEPA residual-health idea inside the row gate itself. The candidates are mostly ultra-low-bad diagnostics around the efgate/backoff manifold, not replacements for the actual-anchor frontier.

## LeJEPA SIGReg Residual-Health Addendum

This addendum applies the LeJEPA non-degeneracy idea to row-level logit residual embeddings. Lower `lejepa_residual_health` means the residual move is less collapsed/anisotropic under random-projection Gaussian tests. Use this as a regularizer on top of actual-anchor, posterior, raw-axis, and bad-axis checks, not as a standalone submission score.

## Decision Rule

- If one JEPA candidate can be submitted, prefer rank 1 for upside, rank 2 for low-bad balance, or rank 3 for strict raw05-axis neutrality.
- Treat `actual_probe_s1_raw` target-assembly rows as high-upside probes only: they slightly improve the actual-anchor proxy, but they raise posterior/bad-axis risk.
- Treat `pair_q2_s1_raw` rows as compromise probes: they keep most of the S1 raw actual-anchor upside while using Q2 raw to cut bad-axis exposure.
- Treat `conservative_q2_raw` rows as risk reducers: they give up a tiny amount of actual-anchor score while sharply lowering bad-axis exposure.
- Treat `q3boost_actual_probe` target-weight rows as the newest high-upside JEPA probe: actual-anchor improves, but posterior proxy is less safe than the main rank-1 candidate.
- Treat `q3stress_raw_boundary` rows as the safer edge of that high-upside branch: Q3 is boosted harder, while raw05-axis and bad-axis constraints are still just inside the guardrail.
- Treat `q3cw_actual_probe` rows as the cleaner Q3-stress compromise: slightly weaker actual-anchor than raw Q3 stress, but much lower bad-axis through non-Q3/S4 counterweighting.
- Treat `q3cwlocal_actual_probe` rows as the refined cleaner branch: they improve posterior/bad-axis versus the coarse counterweight while staying near the Q3-stress actual-anchor frontier.
- Treat `q3cwlocal_raw_boundary` or `q3cwlocal_strict_raw` rows as the guardrail variants when raw05-axis drift must stay under `1e-7` or below zero.
- Treat `q3cwlocal_very_low_bad` rows as diagnostic probes for whether public rewards the lowest bad-axis more than the best actual-anchor proxy.
- Treat `ctxenergy_*` rows as JEPA compatibility guardrails: they lower context-target energy and raw-axis drift, but they do not replace the local counterweight actual-anchor frontier.
- Treat `energyfront_actual_frontier` rows as the current raw05-compatible JEPA frontier: they preserve Q3-stress structure while cutting bad-axis to roughly `8e-4`.
- Treat `energyfront_energy_improved` and `energyfront_strict_raw` rows as the guarded variants when context-target energy or non-positive raw drift is required.
- Treat `efmicro_actual_lowbad` rows as second-stage bad-axis compensation probes: they give up only tiny actual-anchor margin while cutting bad-axis to roughly `4e-4`-`5e-4`.
- Treat `efmicro_energy_improved` and `efmicro_strict_lowbad` rows as diagnostic guardrails when row-level JEPA/bad-axis gates are more important than the best actual-anchor proxy.
- Treat `efgate_actual_guarded` rows as smooth posterior/low-bad diagnostics: q1light soft gates lower posterior and bad-axis but do not beat the micro actual frontier.
- Treat `efgate_ultralow_bad` and `efgate_raw_tight` rows as stress tests for whether public strongly rewards bad-axis collapse down to about `5e-5`.
- Treat `efback_actual_compromise` rows as risk-none middle points between micro and efgate: they give up actual-anchor margin to lower posterior and bad-axis.
- Treat `efback_ultralow_bad` rows as the strongest bad-axis stress tests, with some rows below `4e-5`.
- Treat `siggate_*` rows as LeJEPA-gated stress diagnostics: they can push bad-axis near zero while preserving raw-tightness, but current actual-anchor is weaker than efmicro/energyfront.
- Treat `siganchor_*` rows as compromise probes between efmicro and siggate: they recover most actual-anchor strength while lowering posterior/bad-axis versus the efmicro posterior-safe row, but they do not beat the efmicro frontier.
- Treat `axistrade_*` rows as the strongest direct motif/posterior repair probes so far: they satisfy the high-retention, posterior-safe, raw-tight tradeoff constraint, but their local edge versus raw05 is still below the local proxy resolution.
- Treat LeJEPA SIGReg as residual-health regularization: it demotes one-axis/anisotropic moves even when their actual-anchor proxy is strong.
- If optimizing actual-anchor only, `energyfront_a190aa25` remains the frontier; if choosing the most JEPA-balanced probe, prefer `efmicro_1859bae9` or `efmicro_9f19106d` before the more extreme efgate/backoff stress tests.
- Treat `target_weight_low_bad` rows as the cleaner Q2/S1 attenuation variant when bad-axis exposure matters.
- If preserving known public performance is more important than exploring new JEPA signal, raw05 remains the observed score to beat.
- Do not submit direct JEPA latent residual/Q2-forced variants without an explicit raw05-axis counter; observed public feedback already rejected that direction.

## Cross-View JEPA Surprise LB Audit Addendum

- `analysis_outputs/cross_view_jepa_surprise_combo_builder.py` found a strong local representation family: best combo `cvjepa_surprise_full_nonq2` improves stage2 OOF from `0.5675309247` to `0.5646068482`, with subject-half delta `-0.0029323116` and geometry delta `-0.0034774605`.
- `analysis_outputs/cross_view_jepa_surprise_lb_proxy_audit.py` rejects the large OOF-gain rows as raw05-safe replacements. The best submission-space risk row is `submission_cvjepa_surprise_full_nonq2_w020.csv`, but its raw05-relative proxy is `0.5777849699`, delta `+0.0002586627` versus raw05 public `0.5775263072`.
- The full-strength row `submission_cvjepa_surprise_full_nonq2.csv` has stronger OOF but local public-proxy risk is high: raw05-relative proxy `0.5782543353`, delta `+0.0007280281`, and model spread `0.0008285982`.
- Decision: treat cross-view JEPA surprise as a feature discovery and public information probe, not as the current conservative submit leader. Only `submission_cvjepa_surprise_full_nonq2_w020.csv` is worth submitting from this branch, and only after raw05-compatible e40/lowbad candidates if submission budget allows.

## Raw05-Compatible CVJEPA Frontier Refine Addendum

- `analysis_outputs/raw05_cvjepa_surprise_micro_graft.py` tested direct raw05 injections of capped `cvjepa - stage2` logit residuals. Best local-proxy row was `submission_raw05_cvjepa_surprise_graft_c3d9cd3d.csv` with raw05-relative delta `-0.0000010228`, but actual-anchor stayed at `0.5779067907`; this is a tiny information probe, not a frontier candidate.
- `analysis_outputs/frontier_cvjepa_surprise_micro_refine.py` then injected the same residual family into existing raw05-compatible frontier anchors. This is the useful branch.
- High-upside actual-anchor cvjepa-frontier probe:
  `submission_frontier_cvjepa_refine_a2c8d2c8.csv`
  actual-anchor `0.5778270682`, posterior `0.5768966986`, raw-axis delta `0.0000000725`, bad-axis `0.0001202771`, raw05-relative proxy delta `-0.0000033478`.
- Strict raw / low-bad cvjepa-frontier probe:
  `submission_frontier_cvjepa_refine_b1d38df6.csv`
  actual-anchor `0.5778275958`, posterior `0.5769038478`, raw-axis delta `0.0000000986`, bad-axis `-0.0000008961`, raw05-relative proxy delta `-0.0000040617`.
- Ultra-low-bad information probe:
  `submission_frontier_cvjepa_refine_e725a22f.csv`
  actual-anchor `0.5778277704`, posterior `0.5769058973`, raw-axis delta `0.0000001872`, bad-axis `0.0000000002`, raw05-relative proxy delta `-0.0000041086`.
- Decision: these do not exceed local LB resolution, but they are better-structured than the stage2-family cvjepa submissions. If testing one cvjepa-derived candidate after e40/lowbad, prefer `a2c8d2c8` for actual-anchor upside or `b1d38df6` for strict raw/low-bad balance. Use `e725a22f` only as a bad-axis-collapse diagnostic.

## Public Result / Bottleneck Addendum After A2C8

- Submitted `submission_frontier_cvjepa_refine_a2c8d2c8.csv`; public LB `0.577439321`.
- This is now the observed best, improving raw05 `0.5775263072` by `-0.0000869862`.
- The local raw05-relative proxy predicted `0.5775229594`, so it got the direction right but undercalled the gain by `0.0000836384`.
- The old six-anchor leave-one-anchor proxy fails this family: its signed-axis prediction for `a2c8` is `0.5778666938`, an error of `+0.0004273728`.
- New best 7-anchor leave-one-anchor MAE is still `0.0002979250`; this remains above nearly all candidate edges, so local candidate ordering is not fine enough for confident 1e-4 decisions.
- Distance from `a2c8` to `0.54` is `0.037439321`; the raw05 -> `a2c8` gain covers only `0.2323%` of that gap.
- `a2c8` mean absolute move vs raw05 is `0.0016463907`; even the all-directions-correct best-case logloss gain is only `0.0050731896` (`13.55%` of the 0.54 gap).

Decision update:

- Keep `a2c8` as the current observed anchor, not merely a candidate.
- Treat `b1d38df6` and `e725a22f` as same-family diagnostics rather than obvious next submits; they are locally a few micro-points better than `a2c8`, but the family-level proxy uncertainty is much larger.
- The main bottleneck is no longer feature discovery alone. It is evaluation/transfer: local JEPA features improve OOF, but public-safe moves are too small and the public-anchor calibrator is too underdetermined.
- To attack 0.54, prioritize hidden subset/label inference or larger JEPA representation moves with explicit public-axis stress testing. Raw05-compatible micro-refines are now calibration probes.

## Public Inverse7 Blend Addendum

New scripts:

- `analysis_outputs/public_lb_inverse_mask_audit_7anchor.py`
- `analysis_outputs/public_lb_inverse7_next_probe_selector.py`
- `analysis_outputs/public_lb_inverse7_blend_probe_builder.py`

Local validation:

- Selected files all pass row count, key-order, probability range, and NaN checks.
- The 7-anchor inverse mask now includes `a2c8` public `0.577439321`, so candidate scoring is conditioned on both good anchors (`raw05`, `a2c8`) and the rejected JEPA latent probes.
- Top inverse masks concentrate on `id01` and early `id01/id02` blocks, not the whole test set. This makes target-masked, subset-aware probes more rational than global recalibration.

Updated next-submit priority:

1. `submission_inverse7blend_1040423d.csv`
   - Best information-rich probe.
   - `a2c8 -> public_entropy_g075`, target `no_q2`, weight `0.15`, cap `0.010`.
   - raw05+a2c8-compatible inverse delta `-0.000050403`; full inverse delta `-0.000429297`; orth ratio to a2c8 `0.725322`.

2. `submission_inverse7blend_404221a2.csv`
   - Safer public-entropy sibling.
   - `public_entropy_g050`, target `no_q2`, weight `0.15`, cap `0.010`.
   - compat delta `-0.000047909`; full delta `-0.000380225`; orth ratio `0.756231`.

3. `submission_inverse7blend_bccfd24d.csv`
   - Lower-weight no-Q2 diagnostic.
   - `public_entropy_g075`, target `no_q2`, weight `0.10`, cap `0.010`.
   - compat delta `-0.000045535`; full delta `-0.000330231`.

4. `submission_inverse7blend_b32dd1a5.csv`
   - Conservative q3/s-stage axis probe.
   - donor `public6q3s4corr_energyfront`, target `q3_s2_s3_s4`, weight `0.25`, cap `0.004`.
   - compat delta `-0.000000084`, full delta `+0.000001551`; very low risk, very low information.

5. `submission_inverse7blend_3f238743.csv`
   - Same-family cvjepa control.
   - donor `frontier_cvjepa_refine_80e9f7f8`, target `q3_s2_s4`, weight `1.00`, cap `0.004`.
   - compat delta `-0.000000349`, full delta `-0.000000074`; likely too small to matter, useful as a control only.

Decision update:

- If the next public submission is meant to answer the bottleneck question, submit `submission_inverse7blend_1040423d.csv`.
- If the next public submission must be low-risk, submit `submission_inverse7blend_b32dd1a5.csv`, but do not expect a large move.
- Do not keep spending budget on tiny same-family cvjepa deltas unless the goal is calibration. They are below local/public uncertainty and cannot explain a path to 0.54.
- The practical modification is to use a2c8 as the observed anchor and test capped, no-Q2, hidden-block-aware JEPA/public-entropy blends. The strategic modification is to move from micro-refinement to hidden subset/label inference or a much stronger JEPA representation.

## Target-Ablation Sparse Scale Probe Addendum

New script:

- `analysis_outputs/jepa_target_ablation_scale_probe.py`

Outputs:

- `analysis_outputs/jepa_target_ablation_scale_probe_report.md`
- `analysis_outputs/jepa_target_ablation_scale_probe_scan.csv`
- `analysis_outputs/jepa_target_ablation_scale_probe_actual_anchor.csv`
- `analysis_outputs/jepa_target_ablation_scale_probe_cv_summary.csv`
- `analysis_outputs/jepa_target_ablation_scale_probe_selected.csv`

Validation:

- Script compiles with the sparse scale-ladder and adaptive solver scripts.
- The 20 selected target-ablation submissions match the sample submission shape, column order, and key order.
- Selected probability range is finite and inside `[0, 1]`: min `0.0630798631`, max `0.9797988457`.
- `submission_targetabl_64102eec.csv`, `submission_targetabl_25d719c0.csv`, and `submission_targetabl_8f81d324.csv` are exactly identical to the existing scale-ladder files `submission_sparseladder_b01acaa1.csv`, `submission_sparseladder_89817541.csv`, and `submission_sparseladder_f1ee16b0.csv` respectively.

Main finding:

- The cleanest public-axis proxy is not a single label. It is a coupled Q3/stage region:
  - `submission_targetabl_b19056bb.csv`: `q3_stage`, actual-anchor `0.577727`, honest CV delta `-0.000552`, mean move `0.004452`.
  - `submission_targetabl_1049b8e7.csv`: `q3_s2_s3_s4`, actual-anchor `0.577738`, honest CV delta `-0.000580`, mean move `0.004809`.
- The larger-move score probes remain the all/no-Q2 scale-ladder directions:
  - `submission_sparseladder_b01acaa1.csv`: actual-anchor `0.577746`, honest CV delta `-0.000935`, mean move `0.008816`.
  - `submission_sparseladder_89817541.csv`: actual-anchor `0.577757`, honest CV delta `-0.001013`, mean move `0.009260`.
  - `submission_sparseladder_f1ee16b0.csv`: actual-anchor `0.577758`, honest CV delta `-0.000934`, mean move `0.008276`.
- True single-target movement is weak. Best single-target probes are Q3-only around actual-anchor `0.577787` with mean move only about `0.0024`; Q1-only is weaker. This argues that the hidden axis is target-coupled, not separable by one label.

Decision update:

- Target-ablation does not replace the scale-ladder priority; it explains it.
- For score-oriented public probing, keep the first-submit priority on `submission_sparseladder_b01acaa1.csv`, `submission_sparseladder_89817541.csv`, or `submission_sparseladder_f1ee16b0.csv`.
- For diagnostic target leakage, submit `submission_targetabl_b19056bb.csv` before any single-target probe. It tests the clean Q3/stage edge with lower move amplitude.
- Do not promote adaptive scale candidates until a public result identifies which target/block is leaking; adaptive improved hidden-label CV but worsened actual-anchor.

## Inverse7-Gated Sparse Scale Addendum

New script:

- `analysis_outputs/jepa_inverse7_gated_sparse_scale.py`

Outputs:

- `analysis_outputs/jepa_inverse7_gated_sparse_scale_report.md`
- `analysis_outputs/jepa_inverse7_gated_sparse_scale_scan.csv`
- `analysis_outputs/jepa_inverse7_gated_sparse_scale_actual_anchor.csv`
- `analysis_outputs/jepa_inverse7_gated_sparse_scale_cv_summary.csv`
- `analysis_outputs/jepa_inverse7_gated_sparse_scale_selected.csv`

Experiment:

- Take the sparse JEPA/direct-label logit directions.
- Gate them by inverse7 public-hidden row masks: `id01`, `prefix20`, `prefix30`, subject-prefix, and weighted top-mask posterior gates.
- Test whether public-split row localization can preserve scale while reducing leakage.

Result:

- Generated `960` candidates.
- Best row gate is `prefix30`; single-subject `id01` is too low-amplitude.
- Best selected diagnostics:
  - `submission_inv7gate_a3613347.csv`: `prefix30/q3_stage`, actual-anchor `0.577855`, honest CV delta `-0.000290`, mean move `0.002401`.
  - `submission_inv7gate_0a9c0c66.csv`: `prefix30/all`, actual-anchor `0.577886`, honest CV delta `-0.000351`, mean move `0.003308`.
  - `submission_inv7gate_31adfb5b.csv`: `inv64_soft/all`, actual-anchor `0.577914`, honest CV delta `-0.000310`, mean move `0.004254`.
- Selected diagnostic files pass submission integrity checks.

Decision update:

- Row-gated sparse scale does not beat uniform scale-ladder and should not be submitted first.
- Inverse7 row masks are currently better as diagnostics than as hard construction gates.
- Keep `submission_inv7gate_0a9c0c66.csv` only as a later public-block diagnostic if the scale-ladder result suggests prefix-row leakage.

## Bad-Axis Orthogonal Scale-Ladder Addendum

New script:

- `analysis_outputs/jepa_bad_axis_orthogonal_scale_ladder.py`

Outputs:

- `analysis_outputs/jepa_bad_axis_orthogonal_scale_ladder_report.md`
- `analysis_outputs/jepa_bad_axis_orthogonal_scale_ladder_scan.csv`
- `analysis_outputs/jepa_bad_axis_orthogonal_scale_ladder_cv_detail.csv`
- `analysis_outputs/jepa_bad_axis_orthogonal_scale_ladder_cv_summary.csv`
- `analysis_outputs/jepa_bad_axis_orthogonal_scale_ladder_selected.csv`

Experiment:

- Start from the useful sparse scale-ladder directions.
- Remove active-gate logit components aligned with known public-failed directions:
  - `anchor578`
  - `ordinal_q`
  - `jepa_bad_residual`
  - `jepa_bad_q2`
  - failed direct-consensus axes
- Test whether the remaining orthogonal residual preserves amplitude while reducing public-axis risk.

Result:

- `jepa_bad2` projection is mostly a no-op on the top sparse directions: the best selected rows have removed ratio `0`.
- Non-zero projection against `public_bad4` or `classic_bad2` is possible, but it hurts the actual-anchor frontier:
  - `submission_ortholadder_cc4d9154.csv`: actual-anchor `0.577782`, honest CV delta `-0.000795`, mean move `0.007940`.
  - `submission_ortholadder_8ef88723.csv`: actual-anchor `0.577794`, honest CV delta `-0.000823`, mean move `0.008355`.
- These are worse than unorthogonalized f465 scale rows:
  - f465 full scale `1.30`: actual-anchor `0.577724`, honest CV delta `-0.000919`.
  - f465 full scale `1.50`: actual-anchor `0.577757`, honest CV delta `-0.001013`.
- Six diagnostic ortholadder files were written and passed shape/key/probability checks.

Decision update:

- Do not submit the ortholadder family before the existing scale-ladder priority rows.
- The bad public anchors are not pure bad directions. Their global logit components contain signal useful to actual-anchor, so naive orthogonal projection is too blunt.
- Keep the score priority unchanged:
  1. `analysis_outputs/submission_sparseladder_b01acaa1.csv`
  2. `analysis_outputs/submission_sparseladder_89817541.csv`
  3. `analysis_outputs/submission_sparseladder_f1ee16b0.csv`
- Next useful work: decompose failed axes by row block and target group, or infer hidden label priors directly. Do not spend more time on global bad-axis projection unless public feedback specifically points there.

## Blockwise Bad-Axis Decomposition Addendum

New script:

- `analysis_outputs/jepa_blockwise_bad_axis_decomposition.py`

Outputs:

- `analysis_outputs/jepa_blockwise_bad_axis_decomposition_report.md`
- `analysis_outputs/jepa_blockwise_bad_axis_decomposition_scan.csv`
- `analysis_outputs/jepa_blockwise_bad_axis_decomposition_cv_detail.csv`
- `analysis_outputs/jepa_blockwise_bad_axis_decomposition_cv_summary.csv`
- `analysis_outputs/jepa_blockwise_bad_axis_decomposition_selected.csv`

Experiment:

- Keep the useful sparse JEPA/direct-label move globally.
- Remove failed public-axis components only inside row-block and target-group gates instead of projecting them out globally.
- Test inverse7-style row gates (`id01`, early prefixes, subject prefixes/suffixes, inverse posterior gates), target groups (`all`, `no_q2`, `q3_stage`, `q3_s2_s3_s4`, `stage_all`), and failed-axis groups (`classic_bad2`, `public_bad4`, `consensus_bad3`, `all_bad7`).

Result:

- Scored `365` blockwise candidates and selected `9` diagnostic submissions.
- Selected files pass shape, key-order, finite probability, and range checks.
- Best row:
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_blockorth_3a28f87f.csv`
  - source `282_consensus_directrob`, target `full`, row gate `rowmod4_rem3`, correction target `stage_all`, axis group `public_bad4`, anti lambda `0.35`, signed projection, scale `1.30`
  - actual-anchor `0.577744`, honest CV delta `-0.000892`, worst CV delta `-0.000674`, robust delta vs a2c8 `-0.001141`, mean move `0.008599`, removed norm ratio `0.475478`
- Close sibling:
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_blockorth_0352b65f.csv`
  - row gate `prefix30`, correction target `no_q2`, actual-anchor `0.577744`, honest CV delta `-0.000884`, mean move `0.008585`

Comparison:

- Blockwise projection is materially better than the global ortholadder family.
- It is still only a marginal sibling of the existing scale-ladder frontier:
  - `submission_blockorth_3a28f87f.csv`: actual-anchor `0.577744`, honest CV delta `-0.000892`, mean move `0.008599`
  - `submission_sparseladder_b01acaa1.csv`: actual-anchor `0.577746`, honest CV delta `-0.000935`, mean move `0.008816`
  - `submission_sparseladder_89817541.csv`: actual-anchor `0.577757`, honest CV delta `-0.001013`, mean move `0.009260`
- The actual-anchor edge over `b01acaa1` is only about `0.000002`, while CV/robust support is slightly weaker. This is below the local proxy uncertainty and should not be treated as a resolved score improvement.

Decision update:

- Add `analysis_outputs/submission_blockorth_3a28f87f.csv` as a near-frontier diagnostic sibling of `submission_sparseladder_b01acaa1.csv`.
- Keep the score-first submission priority unchanged:
  1. `analysis_outputs/submission_sparseladder_b01acaa1.csv`
  2. `analysis_outputs/submission_sparseladder_89817541.csv`
  3. `analysis_outputs/submission_sparseladder_f1ee16b0.csv`
- Use `submission_blockorth_3a28f87f.csv` if public feedback suggests stage-specific bad-axis leakage or if `b01acaa1` is unexpectedly weak.
- The strategic bottleneck remains hidden subset/label-prior identification. Projection repair now gives marginal local movement; it does not create the scale needed for a 0.54 path.

## Sparse Direction Ensemble Orthogonalizer Addendum

New script:

- `analysis_outputs/jepa_sparse_direction_ensemble_orthogonalizer.py`

Outputs:

- `analysis_outputs/jepa_sparse_direction_ensemble_orthogonalizer_report.md`
- `analysis_outputs/jepa_sparse_direction_ensemble_orthogonalizer_scan.csv`
- `analysis_outputs/jepa_sparse_direction_ensemble_orthogonalizer_cv_detail.csv`
- `analysis_outputs/jepa_sparse_direction_ensemble_orthogonalizer_cv_summary.csv`
- `analysis_outputs/jepa_sparse_direction_ensemble_orthogonalizer_selected.csv`

Experiment:

- Instead of subtracting failed public axes from one direction, combine the strongest sparse directions in logit space and then optionally apply bad-axis projection.
- Source directions include `b01acaa1`, `89817541`, `f1ee16b0`, `blockorth_3a28f87f`, and the Q3/stage target-ablation direction.
- This tests whether the frontier is limited by single-source mixture error rather than a removable bad-axis component.

Result:

- Generated `2604` unique direction-ensemble candidates, prefiltered `357`, and anchor-CV scored `130`.
- Selected `24` submissions; all pass shape, key-order, finite probability, and range checks.
- New best local larger-move frontier:
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_direns_2a96ae73.csv`
  - blend: `submission_sparseladder_b01acaa1.csv` + `submission_blockorth_3a28f87f.csv` + `submission_targetabl_b19056bb.csv`
  - weights `0.33/0.33/0.33`, full target, all cells, no explicit bad-axis projection, scale `1.10`
  - actual-anchor `0.577729`, honest CV delta `-0.000877`, worst CV delta `-0.000648`, robust delta vs a2c8 `-0.001112`, mean move `0.008015`
- Close score probes:
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_direns_1e0f159d.csv`: `b01 + blockorth + f1ee`, equal weights, scale `0.95`, actual-anchor `0.577729`, honest CV `-0.000898`, move `0.008133`
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_direns_c0fdb76b.csv`: `b01 + f1ee`, weights `0.65/0.35`, scale `0.95`, actual-anchor `0.577731`, honest CV `-0.000911`, move `0.008196`
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_direns_c4af1fd8.csv`: `b01 + 898 + f1ee`, weights `0.50/0.25/0.25`, scale `0.95`, actual-anchor `0.577733`, honest CV `-0.000930`, move `0.008353`
- Orthogonalized ensemble diagnostics are still weaker:
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_direns_b0962ff8.csv`: `public_bad4` anti `0.25`, removed ratio `0.334509`, actual-anchor `0.577760`, honest CV `-0.000826`, move `0.008030`
  - This is useful as a diagnostic but not a score-first replacement.

Decision update:

- Promote `analysis_outputs/submission_direns_2a96ae73.csv` to the first score-oriented public probe. It improves the local actual-anchor frontier by about `0.000017` versus `b01acaa1` while staying in the larger-move band.
- Keep `analysis_outputs/submission_direns_1e0f159d.csv` and `analysis_outputs/submission_direns_c4af1fd8.csv` as close siblings. `c4af1fd8` has stronger honest CV but slightly weaker actual-anchor.
- Keep `analysis_outputs/submission_sparseladder_89817541.csv` as the high-scale stress probe. It still has larger mean move and stronger honest CV, but weaker actual-anchor.
- Do not promote the explicit orthogonalized ensemble rows before the non-orthogonal ensemble rows. Bad-axis subtraction again looks like a diagnostic, not the frontier.
- Updated score-first order:
  1. `analysis_outputs/submission_direns_2a96ae73.csv`
  2. `analysis_outputs/submission_direns_1e0f159d.csv`
  3. `analysis_outputs/submission_direns_c4af1fd8.csv`
  4. `analysis_outputs/submission_sparseladder_89817541.csv`
  5. `analysis_outputs/submission_sparseladder_f1ee16b0.csv`

Strategic interpretation:

- The best new movement came from JEPA/direct-label direction ensembling, not from stronger bad-axis orthogonalization.
- This means the immediate bottleneck is mixture/scale selection among partially correct hidden-structure directions.
- The 0.54 path still requires hidden subset/label-prior identification, but the best next public probe is now the direction ensemble because it is a larger move with the best current actual-anchor stress.

## Direction Ensemble Combo-Stress Correction

New stress audit:

- `analysis_outputs/jepa_direction_ensemble_combo_stress_audit.py`
- report: `analysis_outputs/jepa_direction_ensemble_combo_stress_report.md`
- detail: `analysis_outputs/jepa_direction_ensemble_combo_stress_detail.csv`
- summary: `analysis_outputs/jepa_direction_ensemble_combo_stress_summary.csv`
- pairwise: `analysis_outputs/jepa_direction_ensemble_combo_stress_pairwise.csv`

Method:

- Score each candidate on every inverse public scenario/mask combo instead of only using the averaged actual-anchor score.
- Compare pairwise against `b01_ladder`, `898_ladder`, `blockorth_3a28`, and a2c8.
- Use combo weighted delta, weighted win rate, p90 delta, and worst delta to detect average-only artifacts.

Key result:

- `submission_direns_2a96ae73.csv` remains the best actual-anchor average row, but it has weaker combo tails versus `b01_ladder`:
  - weighted delta vs `b01_ladder`: `-0.000009`
  - weighted win rate: `0.562397`
  - p90 delta: `+0.000044`
  - worst delta: `+0.000101`
- `submission_direns_c4af1fd8.csv` is the more robust public probe:
  - weighted delta vs `b01_ladder`: `-0.000011`
  - weighted win rate: `0.634403`
  - p90 delta: `+0.000007`
  - worst delta: `+0.000035`
  - weighted delta vs `898_ladder`: `-0.000009`
  - honest CV delta: `-0.000930`
  - mean move vs a2c8: `0.008353`
- Per-combo-set stress:
  - `direns_c4af` beats `b01_ladder` strongly on `all_sign` (`-0.000024`, win rate `1.0`).
  - It is near-neutral on `inverse_top` (`+0.000005`) rather than failing hard.
  - It beats `b01_ladder` on `raw05_compatible` (`-0.000015`, weighted win rate `0.857751`).

Corrected decision:

- Promote `analysis_outputs/submission_direns_c4af1fd8.csv` to the first robust score-oriented public probe.
- Keep `analysis_outputs/submission_direns_2a96ae73.csv` as the actual-anchor-best sibling, but not the most robust first submit.
- Updated score-first order:
  1. `analysis_outputs/submission_direns_c4af1fd8.csv`
  2. `analysis_outputs/submission_direns_2a96ae73.csv`
  3. `analysis_outputs/submission_direns_c0fdb76b.csv`
  4. `analysis_outputs/submission_direns_1e0f159d.csv`
  5. `analysis_outputs/submission_sparseladder_89817541.csv`
  6. `analysis_outputs/submission_sparseladder_f1ee16b0.csv`

Interpretation:

- The direction-ensemble branch survives a stricter combo-level audit, but the exact first choice changes.
- `c4af` is not the best by raw actual-anchor average; it is best by stability across public-hidden scenario families.
- The remaining bottleneck is still hidden subset/label-prior identification because the robust ensemble edge over `b01` is only about `1e-5` locally.

## Direction Mixture Minimax Optimizer Addendum

New optimizer:

- `analysis_outputs/jepa_direction_mixture_minimax_optimizer.py`
- report: `analysis_outputs/jepa_direction_mixture_minimax_optimizer_report.md`
- selected: `analysis_outputs/jepa_direction_mixture_minimax_optimizer_selected.csv`
- combo summary: `analysis_outputs/jepa_direction_mixture_minimax_optimizer_combo_summary.csv`
- LOO/L2O CV summary: `analysis_outputs/jepa_direction_mixture_minimax_optimizer_cv_summary.csv`

Method:

- Generated deterministic logit-space mixtures from the current sparse/JEPA/direct-label larger-move family.
- Scored `61,630` candidates, actual-anchor rescored `1,800`, combo-stress summarized `190`, and LOO/L2O anchor-CV scored `100`.
- Sources included `b01`, `898`, `f1ee`, `blockorth_3a28`, Q3/stage target-ablation, and `direns_c4af`.
- The objective explicitly compared candidates against `b01_ladder`, `898_ladder`, and `direns_c4af`.

Key result:

- Best new stress probe:
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_mixmin_0c916bb4.csv`
  - blend `direns_c4af + 898_ladder`, weights `0.350/0.650`, full target, all rows/cells, no projection, scale `0.95`
  - actual-anchor `0.577734`, mean move vs a2c8 `0.008496`
  - combo weighted delta vs `b01_ladder`: `-0.000012877`
  - combo weighted win vs `b01_ladder`: `0.978659`
  - combo p90 delta vs `b01_ladder`: `-0.000008452`
  - combo worst delta vs `b01_ladder`: `+0.000010139`
  - combo weighted delta vs `direns_c4af`: `-0.000001636`
  - honest CV delta mean/worst: `-0.000952` / `-0.000696`
- Close selected siblings:
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_mixmin_5a4c25e0.csv`
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_mixmin_f0d12643.csv`
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_mixmin_f6c04249.csv`
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_mixmin_ef4b1c19.csv`
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_mixmin_7f9cb635.csv`
  - `analysis_outputs/submission_mixmin_615da9a7.csv`

Negative result:

- The best `public_bad4` projection row in the combo pool has actual-anchor only `0.577752` and positive combo delta vs `b01_ladder` about `+0.000016`.
- Row gates and JEPA energy gates also did not survive: best all-row/all-cell/no-projection actual-anchor is `0.577734`, while `rawcompat_soft` and `allsign_soft` start around `0.577750`, and `energy_top70` around `0.577794`.

Decision update:

- Keep `analysis_outputs/submission_direns_c4af1fd8.csv` as the robust existing direction-ensemble reference.
- Add `analysis_outputs/submission_mixmin_0c916bb4.csv` as the first new c4af-stress public probe because it improves combo-tail behavior versus both `b01_ladder` and `direns_c4af`, despite being roughly tied/slightly weaker on averaged actual-anchor.
- Updated probe order:
  1. `analysis_outputs/submission_mixmin_0c916bb4.csv`
  2. `analysis_outputs/submission_direns_c4af1fd8.csv`
  3. `analysis_outputs/submission_mixmin_5a4c25e0.csv`
  4. `analysis_outputs/submission_mixmin_f6c04249.csv`
  5. `analysis_outputs/submission_direns_2a96ae73.csv`
  6. `analysis_outputs/submission_sparseladder_89817541.csv`

Interpretation:

- The optimizer confirms the bottleneck is not generic feature engineering or direct bad-axis subtraction.
- The only surviving larger-move family is still all-row/full-target sparse direction mixture. Hidden subset gates, raw05-compatible row gates, JEPA energy gates, and explicit bad-axis projection currently reduce transfer.
- This is a useful frontier probe, but it is still a `1e-6` to `1e-5` local improvement over `c4af`, not a 0.54-scale breakthrough. A real 0.54 path still needs a new hidden subset/label-prior identification signal.
